  <span id="freeText18204766565816228586" style="display:none">This has originally been a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/56951595-paula" rel="nofollow noopener">Paula</a>.<br /><br />It's definitely a book that took me a while to get into - I was not hooked until about 40% in. It sure was <i>interesting</i>, but the amount of information thrown at the reader made it very hard to connect to the plot or the characters. Didn't help that Cheris was on the very bland side. Kind of <i>Malazan</i>-like in that. The worldbuilding is great and quite unique (calendrical heresy!), and once it got going, it was very hard to let go and wait until we were caught up (the eternal curse of buddy reading) and the "holy shit" moments were constant near the end.<br /><br /><b>Enjoyment:</b> 4/5<br /><b>Execution:</b> 4/5<br /><br /><b>Recommended to:</b> sci-fi/science fantasy fans, anyone looking for unique worldbuilding<br /><b>Not recommended to:</b> those who hate technobabble and "sink or swim" worldbuilding<br /><br /><i>More reviews on my blog, <a href="https://otherworldsreviews.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">To Other Worlds</a>.</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1616137988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616137988" />
    <a title="Lata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13126933-lata"><img alt="Lata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525485137p2/13126933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616137988?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lata" href="/user/show/13126933-lata">Lata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781849979924" href="/book/show/30623070-ninefox-gambit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=bipoc-author">bipoc-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=x2017-read">x2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=x2017-sff-tbr-cleanup">x2017-sff-tbr-cleanup</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616137988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16988649832159190883">Strange, weird tech with stranger names for it. Interesting main characters. A story of the hexarchate empire, which is based on ultra-strict adherence to mathematical theories and calculations, and rebellions, based on alternative mathematical models, against the hexarchate. The hexarchate is made up of six factions, one of which, the Kel, which uses mind control with its soldiers. The hexarchate as a whole has a variety of weird weaponry and spaceships, and has experienced horrible violence in</span>
  <span id="freeText16988649832159190883" style="display:none">Strange, weird tech with stranger names for it. Interesting main characters. A story of the hexarchate empire, which is based on ultra-strict adherence to mathematical theories and calculations, and rebellions, based on alternative mathematical models, against the hexarchate. The hexarchate is made up of six factions, one of which, the Kel, which uses mind control with its soldiers. The hexarchate as a whole has a variety of weird weaponry and spaceships, and has experienced horrible violence in its past dealing with uprisings. <br />The main characters are Kel Cheris, a mathematician/soldier, and Shuos Jedao, a centuries-dead, utterly brilliant general. This story begins with a new rebellion against the hexarchate, resulting in "calendrical rot". Cheris proposes using Jedao to fight the rebels; a good portion of the action depends on how Cheris and Jedao function together to deal with the rebellion.<br />There are also sentient artificial beings, known as servitors, that handle any number of activities (e.g., serving food, cleaning, etc.) and watch the developing action, and the behaviour of the humans around them.<br />Ninefox Gambit is not an easy or quick read, but is a good book; the author's language and imagery are beautiful, bizarre and brutal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16988649832159190883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2798970207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798970207" />
    <a title="Chris Berko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13125862-chris-berko"><img alt="Chris Berko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501820241p2/13125862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798970207?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Berko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Berko" href="/user/show/13125862-chris-berko">Chris Berko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798970207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18366496060694026475">Very very very very very... good. Wasn't feeling this at first and almost gave up on it at about the 100 page mark but it started to grow on me. The more I accepted that I would not understand it all the more I enjoyed it and I eventually gave myself up to an author who seemed to know what they were doing and I sat back to enjoy the ride. Reading other reviews I came to see it was written this way on purpose and it was not through some fault of my own that some of the ideas and concepts did not </span>
  <span id="freeText18366496060694026475" style="display:none">Very very very very very... good. Wasn't feeling this at first and almost gave up on it at about the 100 page mark but it started to grow on me. The more I accepted that I would not understand it all the more I enjoyed it and I eventually gave myself up to an author who seemed to know what they were doing and I sat back to enjoy the ride. Reading other reviews I came to see it was written this way on purpose and it was not through some fault of my own that some of the ideas and concepts did not make sense in my brain. There really weren't any dull parts as the pace was pretty relentless and the ending was way cool with enough of a hook that I want to continue the series. Sincerely, the last fifty pages were seriously kick-ass and very well done. I also appreciated the different viewpoints throughout the siege and that it flips from the boots on the ground grunts to the people behind the scenes making the decisions and not only what was happening but the psychological impact all of it had on everyone involved. Very ambitious and self-assured for a debut novel and it gets a lot of cool points for originality. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18366496060694026475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/5663034-k">K.</a>
      </span>

          marked it as did-not-finish


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29503206-ninefox-gambit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=diverse-author">diverse-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=omg-that-cover">omg-that-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=poc-narrator">poc-narrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=setting-space">setting-space</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1927117313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer976750648861399122">DNFed at the 37% mark. <br/><br/>I'd heard so many AMAZING things about this book. Combine that with the stunning cover and the fact that it's sci-fi by an Asian author and I thought this would be a sure fire hit for me. <br/><br/>But when I got to just shy of page 150 and I still had LITERALLY NO IDEA WHAT WAS HAPPENING, I just didn't have the motivation to push on. <br/><br/>Who knows, maybe I'm just too stupid for this book.<br/><br/>Maybe I'll go back to it at some point in the future. But for now, I'm calling it quits. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5r8PKO9CpDxYkAJUqYNMZlillLzzcRnSQw5HYgx3/kKq75qUKPqqi+H0kr56fegzpuYobcvjohikTAGJ3LNZbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0BD99Sp07zwfWeoyn5YUfjStzmCEGkiMMuxS/iHcpaacQGhJ7czhi6Y9ethMaLAryu5ysbyI80bVrhQV8RgCig==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17351902738280942635">Yoon Ha Lee is an American science fiction writer born on January 26, 1979 in Houston, Texas. His first published story, “The Hundredth Question,” appeared in Fantasy & Science Fiction in 1999; since then, over two dozen further stories have appeared. He lives in Baton Rouge, Louisiana.</span>

He lives in Baton Rouge, Louisiana.</span>
